 PREFACE.

 —
 ..ω-

 IT must ever be a subject of dee regret, that, of
 the rich and invaluable treasures of man literature,
 so little has descended to us expressly prepared for the
 use of children, or particularly adapted to lead be in-
 ners, by regular and easy steps, to the knowledge 018 the
 most useful and most interesting of all the languages of
 antiquity. _

 This is an evil, which, ﬁom its nature, admits of no
 complete remedy. Hence, amidst the variety of sub-
 stitutes, which have been introduced into the schools
 of our country, the choice of suitable elemen books
 is found to be one of the principal sources of diﬂiculty
 to the Latin instructer.

 A general conviction seems to prevail, that, in the

 ’ἶ books of this class, the reform' hand is essentially ne—

 ἱῖἶῗῑξζέἐὲῗὲ Ἓὲι ῗὲῗωὲἶὲἐοὲἲέἔῗυῖᾞὲἒῃδέ
 Cicero, have geel) wantognsly mutilated, miden· the pre-
 tence of rendering them more simple and easy to the
 learner, should be for ever banished, and that nothin
 should be admitted inconsistent with the principles 0
 classical purity.

 With the view of contributi something to an im-
 provement so important, this litt e book has been pre-
 pared, and is now res tt‘ully submitted to those whose
 province it is to deci e its merits.
